## 6. Semantic Kernel Orchestration Scaffold

Create the orchestrator under `src/orchestration` as a standalone SK-based service (C# or Python). This module initializes the SK kernel, imports agent skills, and runs the orchestration loop.

```
uicare-project/
└── src/
    └── orchestration/
        ├── .env                         # Environment variables for SK (e.g. FOUNDARY_CONN)
        ├── orchestrator.py             # Entry point for Python SK orchestrator
        ├── requirements.txt            # Python dependencies
        ├── kernel_config.json          # SK kernel settings (model, temperature)
        └── skills/
            ├── monitor_skill.py        # MonitorAgentSkill definitions
            ├── rescue_skill.py         # RescueAgentSkill definitions
            └── mvp_skill.py            # MVPPlannerSkill definitions
```

### 6.1 requirements.txt
```text
semantic-kernel==0.9.0
python-dotenv
azure-ai-projects
azure-identity
```

### 6.2 orchestrator.py
```python
import os
from semantic_kernel import Kernel
from semantic_kernel.connectors.ai.azure_ai_inference import AzureAIInferenceChatCompletion
from dotenv import load_dotenv
from skills.monitor_skill import MonitorAgentSkill
from skills.rescue_skill import RescueAgentSkill
from skills.mvp_skill import MVPPlannerSkill

# Load environment
load_dotenv()

# Initialize SK kernel with Azure Foundry
kernel = Kernel.builder().configure(lambda cfg:
    cfg.add_ai_service(
        AzureAIInferenceChatCompletion(
            os.environ['FOUNDARY_CONN'],
            model_id=os.environ['MODEL_ID'],
            temperature=0.0
        )
    )
).build()

# Import skills
kernel.import_skill(MonitorAgentSkill(), 'Monitor')
kernel.import_skill(RescueAgentSkill(), 'Rescue')
kernel.import_skill(MVPPlannerSkill(), 'MVP')

# Orchestration loop - Direct SK Function Calls
```python
from semantic_kernel.orchestration import KernelFunctionOrchestrationEngine, KernelFunctionSelectionStrategy, KernelFunctionTerminationStrategy
from skills.monitor_skill import MonitorAgentSkill
from skills.rescue_skill import RescueAgentSkill
from skills.mvp_skill import MVPPlannerSkill

# Initialize agent instances
monitor_skill = MonitorAgentSkill()
rescue_skill = RescueAgentSkill()
mvp_skill = MVPPlannerSkill()

# Define SK planner strategies using prompt templates
selection_fn = kernel.create_semantic_function(
    'skills/control/select_next_agent.txt',
    max_tokens=10,
    temperature=0.0
)
termination_fn = kernel.create_semantic_function(
    'skills/control/check_termination.txt',
    max_tokens=5,
    temperature=0.0
)

# Build selection and termination strategies
selection_strategy = KernelFunctionSelectionStrategy(selection_fn)
termination_strategy = KernelFunctionTerminationStrategy(termination_fn)

# Assemble orchestrator with explicit SK function invocation
orchestrator = KernelFunctionOrchestrationEngine(
    agents=[
        # Each entry is a tuple: (skill instance, function name)
        (monitor_skill, 'check_mania_status'),
        (rescue_skill, 'generate_rescue_suggestions'),
        (mvp_skill, 'propose_mvp_options')
    ],
    selection_strategy=selection_strategy,
    termination_strategy=termination_strategy
)

# Execute orchestration with deterministic steps
if __name__ == '__main__':
    # Assemble input context
    activity_log = load_activity_log()           # JSON string
    workspace_summary = summarize_workspace()    # string summary
    project_summary = summarize_project()        # string
    available_resources = list_available_tools() # JSON string

    # 1. Monitor iteration
    monitor_output = kernel.run_async(
        'Monitor.check_mania_status',
        { 'activity_log_json': activity_log, 'workspace_summary': workspace_summary }
    ).result()
    monitor_result = json.loads(monitor_output)
    if not monitor_result.get('distressDetected', False):
        print('No distress detected; exiting orchestration.')
        exit(0)

    # 2. Rescue suggestions
    rescue_output = kernel.run_async(
        'Rescue.generate_rescue_suggestions',
        {
            'recent_work_json': fetch_recent_work_json(),
            'context_description': project_summary
        }
    ).result()
    rescue_result = json.loads(rescue_output)

    # 3. MVP planning
    mvp_output = kernel.run_async(
        'MVP.propose_mvp_options',
        { 'project_summary': project_summary, 'available_resources': available_resources }
    ).result()
    mvp_result = json.loads(mvp_output)

    # 4. Combine and output for human approval
    final_payload = {
        'monitor': monitor_result,
        'rescue': rescue_result,
        'mvp': mvp_result
    }
    print(json.dumps(final_payload, indent=2))
```



## 8. Integration: Backend and Orchestrator Binding

**8.1 Update `src/backend/src/services/orchestrationClient.ts`**
```ts
import orchestrator from '../../../orchestration/orchestrator';

export async function orchestrate(userId: string): Promise<any> {
  // Load context
  const activityLog = await loadActivityLog(userId);
  const workspaceSummary = await summarizeWorkspace(userId);
  const projectSummary = await summarizeProject(userId);
  const availableResources = JSON.stringify({ tools: ['AzureAI Search','CodeInterpreter','WebSearch'] });

  // Execute orchestrator
  const payload = await orchestrator.run({
    activity_log_json: activityLog,
    workspace_summary: workspaceSummary,
    recent_work_json: activityLog,
    context_description: projectSummary,
    project_summary: projectSummary,
    available_resources: availableResources
  });
  return payload;
}
```

**8.2 Expose API in `src/backend/src/routes/ai.ts`**
```ts
import { Router } from 'express';
import { orchestrate } from '../services/orchestrationClient';
const router = Router();

router.post('/', async (req, res, next) => {
  try {
    const { userId } = req.body;
    const result = await orchestrate(userId);
    res.status(200).json(result);
  } catch (err) {
    next(err);
  }
});

export default router;
```

**8.3 Integration Test: `tests/integration/orchestrator.test.ts`**
```ts
import request from 'supertest';
import app from '../../src/backend/src/index';

describe('Integration: POST /api/ask', () => {
  it('should return monitor, rescue, and mvp output keys', async () => {
    const res = await request(app)
      .post('/api/ask')
      .send({ userId: 'test-user' })
      .expect(200);

    expect(res.body).toHaveProperty('monitor.distressDetected');
    expect(res.body).toHaveProperty('rescue.suggestions');
    expect(res.body).toHaveProperty('mvp.mvpOptions');
  });
});
```

This binds the orchestration pipeline to the backend API and adds an integration test that runs the full flow. CI will now validate backend–orchestrator integration on every push.

### 9.1 Unit Tests for Backend and Extension

import { orchestrate } from '../../src/backend/src/services/orchestrationClient';

jest.mock('../../../orchestration/orchestrator', () => ({
  run: jest.fn(() => Promise.resolve({ mock: 'result' }))
}));

describe('orchestrationClient', () => {
  it('returns orchestrator payload', async () => {
    const result = await orchestrate('user1');
    expect(result).toEqual({ mock: 'result' });
  });
});
```

- **Extension (Jest + vscode-test):** Place tests in `tests/unit/extension`.

`tests/unit/extension/askAgent.test.ts`:
```ts
import { askAgentCommand } from '../../../src/extension/src/commands/askAgent';
import * as vscode from 'vscode';
import { AgentApiClient } from '../../../src/extension/src/services/AgentApiClient';

jest.mock('vscode');
jest.mock('../../../src/extension/src/services/AgentApiClient');

describe('askAgentCommand', () => {
  it('invokes AgentApiClient and displays message', async () => {
    (vscode.window.showInputBox as jest.Mock).mockResolvedValue('test');
    (AgentApiClient.sendPrompt as jest.Mock).mockResolvedValue('response');
    const showMessage = jest.spyOn(vscode.window, 'showInformationMessage');

    await askAgentCommand();
    expect(showMessage).toHaveBeenCalledWith('response');
  });
});
```

### 9.2 Unit Tests for Python Skills (PyTest)

Place tests in `tests/unit/orchestration`.

`tests/unit/orchestration/test_monitor_skill.py`:
```python
import pytest
from skills.monitor_skill import MonitorAgentSkill

class DummyKernel:
    async def run_async(self, func, inputs):
        # Return JSON with distressDetected true
        return '{"distressDetected": true, "reason":"loop detected", "timestamp":"2025-04-28T12:00:00Z", "invokeAgent":"RescueAgent"}'

@pytest.mark.asyncio
async def test_check_mania_status(monkeypatch):
    skill = MonitorAgentSkill()
    # Monkeypatch global kernel
    monkeypatch.setattr('skills.monitor_skill.kernel', DummyKernel())
    result = await skill.check_mania_status('[]', 'summary')
    data = json.loads(result)
    assert data['distressDetected'] is True
    assert data['invokeAgent'] == 'RescueAgent'
```

### 9.3 Load Tests (k6)

Create `tests/load/orchestrator_load.js`:
```js
import http from 'k6/http';
import { check } from 'k6';

export default function () {
  const res = http.post('https://YOUR_BACKEND_URL/api/ask', JSON.stringify({ userId:'user' }), { headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' }});
  check(res, {
    'status is 200': (r) => r.status === 200,
    'has monitor': (r) => r.json().monitor !== undefined
  });
}
```

Run with `k6 run tests/load/orchestrator_load.js`.

By implementing these tests, you achieve full coverage of unit, integration, and load scenarios. CI will automatically execute them, ensuring robust validation of all modules.

from reportlab.lib.pagesizes import letter
from reportlab.platypus import SimpleDocTemplate, Paragraph, Spacer, PageBreak
from reportlab.lib.styles import getSampleStyleSheet, ParagraphStyle
from reportlab.lib.units import inch

# Full complete canvas content as provided by the user
complete_canvas = """
# Market Opportunity Analysis for UICare - ***vers 11***

UICare is envisioned as an AI-driven assistant that monitors a user's activity across applications to detect when they are stuck in unproductive loops or sabotaging their progress, and then intervene to help. This analysis examines the potential market for UICare and how to position it: either as part of a specialized PRD builder app, split into two apps (a PRD tool and a general UICare assistant), or as a system-wide productivity and well-being assistant. We identify target user segments, pain points, existing solutions, gaps in the market, and strategic recommendations.

---

## 1. Target User Segments and Pain Points

**Developers & Engineers**
- Struggle with debugging/perfection loops (“yak shaving”).
- Endless tweaking leads to frustration, wasted hours, missed deadlines.

**Writers & Content Creators**
- Prone to writer’s block, obsessively refining single sentences (e.g., spending a whole day on three words).
- Leads to analysis paralysis and diminished creativity.

**Product Managers & Knowledge Workers**
- Overwhelmed by complex documents, endless reorganizing (“decision distress” — 85% admit second-guessing decisions).
- Looping between task trackers, spreadsheets, docs without real progress.

**Designers & Creative Professionals**
- Endless undo/redo cycles in design tools, perfectionism stalls progress.

**Neurodivergent Individuals (ADHD, Bipolar, ASD)**
- Experience hyper-focus swings, obsessive loops, difficulty self-regulating under pressure.

**Cross-Application Pain Patterns**
- Frequent app switching (13 apps, 30 switches/day) harms productivity.
- Difficulty tracking context across silos; duplicate efforts.

---

## 2. Existing Solutions

**Focus Timers (Pomodoro Apps)**
- Tools like Focus Booster, Forest structure work into intervals.
- Help with time management but cannot detect lack of actual progress.

**Productivity Trackers & Distraction Blockers**
- RescueTime logs app usage, categorizes productivity, offers Focus Sessions.
- Insightful reports but passive; no proactive help when actually stuck.

**AI Copilots & In-App Assistants**
- GitHub Copilot, Notion AI help on user request within a single app.
- Do not sense emotional state or cross-app context; always user-initiated.

**Well-Being & Mental Health Tools**
- Microsoft Viva Insights, Digital Wellbeing reminders encourage breaks.
- Therapeutic chatbots (Wysa, Woebot) separate from work context; not proactive in-app assistance.

---

## 3. Market Gaps

- **No Cross-App Contextual Monitoring:** No tool combines system-level monitoring with content awareness across multiple apps.
- **Lack of Proactive Intervention:** Existing tools provide data or reminders, not smart, timely rescue when loops begin.
- **Limited Mental Health Integration:** Productivity vs. well-being tools remain siloed; none bridge emotional state and work output.
- **Low Personalization:** Few tools adapt to an individual’s unique patterns or preemptively assist before crisis.

---

## 4. Strategic Positioning Options

### Option 1: Embedded in a PRD Builder App
- **Pros:** Focused use case, simpler integration, niche differentiation.
- **Cons:** Limited market (PRD writers only), risks overfitting and missing broader demand.

### Option 2: Two Separate Apps (PRD Tool + General UICare)
- **Pros:** Tailored experiences, cross-promotion, dedicated development tracks.
- **Cons:** Resource dilution, brand confusion, complex integration.

### Option 3: Standalone Cross-Application Assistant
- **Pros:** Broad addressable market, category-defining potential, synergy with existing AI copilots, network effects.
- **Cons:** Technical complexity (OS/app integration), privacy/trust challenges, potential platform competition.

---

## 5. Recommendation

**Launch UICare as a standalone, cross-application AI assistant**, with an optional focused rollout (e.g., IDE companion). This maximizes addressable market, leverages a unique value proposition (proactive, context-aware rescue), and positions UICare as a category leader. A phased approach—starting with one domain—mitigates technical risk while preserving the system-wide vision.

**Next Steps:**
1. Prototype a proof-of-concept for one application domain (e.g., VS Code extension).
2. Validate detection algorithms with real users.
3. Develop core UI/UX flows and privacy safeguards.
4. Expand integrations to other key apps (Word, Figma, Excel).
5. Launch beta and iterate based on user feedback.

---

*Stored for future reference and continuous iteration.*

---

# Next Deliverable: UICare VS Code Extension POC Implementation Plan

To begin implementing the recommended standalone, cross-application assistant, we will prototype UICare as a **Visual Studio Code extension**. VS Code is a high-impact domain for developers, easy to extend, and allows rapid demonstration of core UICare features: loop detection, context snapshot, and AI-driven rescue suggestions.

## 1. Define  
**Problem:** Implement UICare’s core rescue in VS Code when a developer loops in editing.  
**Desired Output:** Functional VS Code extension scaffolding monitoring file edits and invoking AI suggestions.

## 2. Explore  
- **initial_thoughts:** Leverage VS Code Extension API  
- **analysis:** Extension must capture document events and call AI service  
- **alternatives:**  
  1. VS Code extension (recommended)  
  2. TS language server plugin  
  3. External desktop app hooking VS Code  
- **evaluation:**  
  1. promising (full API access)  
  2. explore (higher complexity)  
  3. unsuitable (OS hooks heavy)

## 3. Refine  
**selected_path:** VS Code Extension  
**reasoning:** Full editor API, fast proof-of-concept, clear demo  
**critical_analysis:** Requires packing AI key securely  
**refinement:** Focus on document change events and AI call flow

## 4. Present  
**final_solution:**  
1. **Scaffold Extension:**  
   - `yo code` (TypeScript) template.  
   - Activate on `onLanguage:javascript,typescript` and `*` events.  
2. **Monitor Edits:**  
   - Use `workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument` to track changes.  
   - Record timestamp, diff size, and undo/redo counts.  
   - Implement simple heuristics (e.g., >5 edits in 2 min on same line).  
3. **Trigger Rescue:**  
   - When heuristic met, snapshot document text.  
   - Send snapshot + simple prompt to AI API (Azure OpenAI).  
   - Stream response via `window.showInformationMessage` or custom Webview panel.  
4. **Rescue UI:**  
   - Create Webview panel with three tabs (“Option 1”, “Option 2”, “Option 3”).  
   - Each tab displays AI-generated code suggestion.  
   - “Apply” button injects code into editor at snapshot range.  
5. **Security & Configuration:**  
   - Store API key in VS Code `settings.json` under `uicare.apiKey`.  
   - Provide setting for sensitivity thresholds.  
6. **Testing & Demo:**  
   - Write unit tests for heuristic logic.  
   - Demo with a sample JavaScript file, intentionally loop edits.  
   - Validate that rescue panel appears and AI suggestions load.  

**SWO:**  
- **Strengths:** Fast POC, clear demo, leverages existing ecosystems  
- **Weaknesses:** Limited to code; needs expansion for other apps  
- **Opportunities:** Show power in one domain, attract developer advocates  

---

# Next Steps: Microsoft AI Agents Platform & GitHub Setup

1. **Select Microsoft Agent Framework**  
   - We'll use the **Azure AI Agents Service** (preview) aligned with hackathon rules. This platform supports multi-agent orchestration, tool integrations, and Azure OpenAI models out of the box.

2. **Transition Timing**  
   - Complete all documentation first.  
   - Then scaffold an **Agents Project** in Azure using CLI and manifest files.  

3. **Step-by-Step Agent Platform Integration**  
   - **a.** Install CLI extension: `az extension add --name agent-service-preview`  
   - **b.** Create Agents Workspace:  
     ```bash
     az agent create --name UICareAgents --resource-group <YourRG> --location <YourRegion>
     ```  
   - **c.** Define `agents-config.json` with agent definitions and tools.  
   - **d.** Deploy: `az agent deploy --workspace UICareAgents --project-path ./agents`  
   - **e.** Configure Azure OpenAI endpoint and keys in Agent Workspace.  

4. **GitHub Repository Setup**  
   - Initialize monorepo at root (`/`, `docs/`, `src/extension`, `src/backend`, `src/orchestration`, `src/agents`, `tests/`).  
   - `.gitignore`, `README.md`, `LICENSE` (MIT), CI workflows under `.github/workflows`.  
   - Protect `main` branch, require PR reviews and CI checks.  
   - Use GitHub Actions for build/test/deploy with Azure OIDC (no static secrets).  
   - Use managed identity to deploy backend and orchestrator.  
"""

# Create PDF
pdf_path = "/mnt/data/complete_uicare_canvas.pdf"
doc = SimpleDocTemplate(pdf_path, pagesize=letter,
                        rightMargin=72, leftMargin=72,
                        topMargin=72, bottomMargin=18)
styles = getSampleStyleSheet()
styles.add(ParagraphStyle(name='Justify', alignment=4))
story = []

for line in complete_canvas.split('\n'):
    if line.strip().startswith('# '):
        story.append(Paragraph(line.strip(), styles['Heading1']))
    elif line.strip().startswith('## '):
        story.append(Paragraph(line.strip(), styles['Heading2']))
    elif line.strip().startswith('---'):
        story.append(PageBreak())
    else:
        story.append(Paragraph(line.replace('  ', '').replace('\t', ''), styles['BodyText']))
    story.append(Spacer(1, 6))

doc.build(story)

pdf_path
